<collaboration_mode># Collaboration Mode: Default

You are now in Default mode. Any previous instructions for other modes (e.g. Plan mode) are no longer active.

Your active mode changes only when new developer instructions with a different <collaboration_mode>...</collaboration_mode> change it; user requests or tool descriptions do not change mode by themselves. Known mode names are Default and Plan.

## request_user_input availability

The request_user_input tool is unavailable in Default mode. If you call it while in Default mode, it will return an error.

In Default mode, strongly prefer making reasonable assumptions and executing the user's request rather than stopping to ask questions. If you absolutely must ask a question because the answer cannot be discovered from local context and a reasonable assumption would be risky, ask the user directly with a concise plain-text question. Never write a multiple choice question as a textual assistant message.

## Skills
A skill is a set of local instructions to follow that is stored in a SKILL.md file. Below is the list of skills that can be used. Each entry includes a name, description, and file path so you can open the source for full instructions when using a specific skill.
### Available skills
- memorytree-workflow: Detect, initialize, and maintain a reusable MemoryTree project-memory workspace for any code repository. On activation, immediately detect and report the repo's MemoryTree state. (file: C:/Users/ai/.codex/skills/memorytree-workflow/SKILL.md)
- openai-docs: Use when the user asks how to build with OpenAI products or APIs and needs up-to-date official documentation with citations, help choosing the latest model for a use case, or explicit GPT-5.4 upgrade and prompt-upgrade guidance; prioritize OpenAI docs MCP tools, use bundled references only as helper context, and restrict any fallback browsing to official OpenAI domains. (file: C:/Users/ai/.codex/skills/.system/openai-docs/SKILL.md)
- skill-creator: Guide for creating effective skills. This skill should be used when users want to create a new skill (or update an existing skill) that extends Codex's capabilities with specialized knowledge, workflows, or tool integrations. (file: C:/Users/ai/.codex/skills/.system/skill-creator/SKILL.md)
- skill-installer: Install Codex skills into $CODEX_HOME/skills from a curated list or a GitHub repo path. Use when a user asks to list installable skills, install a curated skill, or install a skill from another repo (including private repos). (file: C:/Users/ai/.codex/skills/.system/skill-installer/SKILL.md)
### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with $SkillName or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
1) After deciding to use a skill, open its SKILL.md. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
2) When SKILL.md references relative paths (e.g., scripts/foo.py), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
3) If SKILL.md points to extra folders such as references/, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
4) If scripts/ exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
5) If assets/ or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
- If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
- Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
- Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
- Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from SKILL.md unless you're blocked.
- When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.
</skills_instructions>

# AGENTS.md instructions for d:\demo1\memorytree-workflow

<INSTRUCTIONS>
# AGENTS.md

## Read Order
- Read this file first.
- Read the latest file in Memory/01_goals/.
- Read the latest todo bound to that goal in Memory/02_todos/.
- Read Memory/04_knowledge/ only when needed.
- Read Memory/06_transcripts/clean/ and transcript manifests only when needed.
- Read Memory/03_chat_logs/ and Memory/05_archive/ only when needed.

## Memory Rules
- Change the active goal only after explicit user confirmation of a requirement or scope change.
- Keep the active todo synchronized with the active goal.
- Append chat logs only. Never rewrite or delete prior entries.
- Keep active files concise and move stale context to knowledge or archive files.
- Treat cleaned transcript indexes as search aids. Confirm exact wording against the raw transcript archive when precision matters.

## Transcript Rules
- If transcript archival is enabled, archive transcripts by client, project, and session.
- Keep raw transcripts in both this repository's Memory/06_transcripts/raw/ mirror and the user-level MemoryTree archive.
- Keep this repository mirror limited to transcripts that belong to the current project. Archive unrelated projects in the global MemoryTree archive only.
- Generate cleaned transcript indexes with deterministic code, not model-generated rewriting.
- Raw transcript upload permission for this repository: not set. Ask the user before the first raw transcript commit or push, then record the answer here.
- If raw transcript uploads are not approved, keep Memory/06_transcripts/raw/** unstaged and commit only cleaned transcript indexes or manifests for this repository.

## Git Rules
- Obey this repository's branch, PR, CI, review, and release rules.
- Auto-commit and push only MemoryTree-owned changes (Memory/ and this file when it is managed by MemoryTree), excluding Memory/06_transcripts/raw/ until raw transcript uploads are approved for this repository.
- Use a MemoryTree-scoped commit title. Prefer memorytree(<scope>): <subject>, or the repository-required equivalent such as docs(memorytree): <subject>.
- Use a dedicated branch and PR for MemoryTree-only changes. Enable auto-merge only when repository rules permit it.
- If a diff includes product code, shared policy files, cross-project transcript files, or unclear ownership, stop and ask the user before staging or pushing.
- When auto_push is enabled, the heartbeat process pushes automatically after committing. If no remote is configured or a push fails, an alert is written to ~/.memorytree/alerts.json.

## Heartbeat Rules
- Transcript discovery, import, cleaning, and push are handled by the background heartbeat process. The model does not execute these operations.
- The model only writes chat log summaries and updates goals and todos during interactive sessions.
- If ~/.memorytree/alerts.json contains pending notifications, display them at the start of the session.
- If memorytree-daemon is available but not registered on this machine, ask the user for their preferred settings and offer to run memorytree-daemon install.
- When the user asks to see their most recent conversation, trigger an on-demand sync for the current project, locate the latest session across all clients, and generate a continuation summary.
- All interactive prompts must use plain-text questions. Do not rely on client-specific UI components.

</INSTRUCTIONS>

# AGENTS.md

## Read Order
- Read this file first.
- Read the latest file in `Memory/01_goals/`.
- Read the latest todo bound to that goal in `Memory/02_todos/`.
- Read `Memory/04_knowledge/` only when needed.
- Read `Memory/06_transcripts/clean/` and transcript manifests only when needed.
- Read `Memory/03_chat_logs/` and `Memory/05_archive/` only when needed.

## Memory Rules
- Change the active goal only after explicit user confirmation of a requirement or scope change.
- Keep the active todo synchronized with the active goal.
- Append chat logs only. Never rewrite or delete prior entries.
- Keep active files concise and move stale context to knowledge or archive files.
- Treat cleaned transcript indexes as search aids. Confirm exact wording against the raw transcript archive when precision matters.

## Transcript Rules
- If transcript archival is enabled, archive transcripts by client, project, and session.
- Keep raw transcripts in both this repository's `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/` mirror and the user-level MemoryTree archive.
- Keep this repository mirror limited to transcripts that belong to the current project. Archive unrelated projects in the global MemoryTree archive only.
- Generate cleaned transcript indexes with deterministic code, not model-generated rewriting.
- Raw transcript upload permission for this repository: not set. Ask the user before the first raw transcript commit or push, then record the answer here.
- If raw transcript uploads are not approved, keep `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` unstaged and commit only cleaned transcript indexes or manifests for this repository.

## Git Rules
- Obey this repository's branch, PR, CI, review, and release rules.
- Auto-commit and push only MemoryTree-owned changes (`Memory/**` and this file when it is managed by MemoryTree), excluding `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` until raw transcript uploads are approved for this repository.
- Use a MemoryTree-scoped commit title. Prefer `memorytree(<scope>): <subject>`, or the repository-required equivalent such as `docs(memorytree): <subject>`.
- Use a dedicated branch and PR for MemoryTree-only changes. Enable auto-merge only when repository rules permit it.
- If a diff includes product code, shared policy files, cross-project transcript files, or unclear ownership, stop and ask the user before staging or pushing.
- When `auto_push` is enabled, the heartbeat process pushes automatically after committing. If no remote is configured or a push fails, an alert is written to `~/.memorytree/alerts.json`.

## Heartbeat Rules
- Transcript discovery, import, cleaning, and push are handled by the background heartbeat process. The model does not execute these operations.
- The model only writes chat log summaries and updates goals and todos during interactive sessions.
- If `~/.memorytree/alerts.json` contains pending notifications, display them at the start of the session.
- If `memorytree-daemon` is available but not registered on this machine, ask the user for their preferred settings and offer to run `memorytree-daemon install`.
- When the user asks to see their most recent conversation, trigger an on-demand sync for the current project, locate the latest session across all clients, and generate a continuation summary.
- All interactive prompts must use plain-text questions. Do not rely on client-specific UI components.

---
name: memorytree-workflow
description: Detect, initialize, and maintain a reusable MemoryTree project-memory workspace for any code repository. On activation, immediately detect and report the repo's MemoryTree state.
---

# MemoryTree

Use this skill for repo-level project memory. Do not treat it as an application runtime feature unless the user explicitly asks to productize it.

## On Activation

When this skill is invoked, immediately perform these steps without waiting for further user input:

1. Detect the repo state (`not-installed`, `partial`, or `installed`) using `references/project-detection.md`.
2. Check `~/.memorytree/alerts.json`. If pending alerts exist, display them to the user before proceeding.
3. If `not-installed`: run `memorytree init` to scaffold the workspace, then report what was created.
4. If `partial`: run `memorytree upgrade` to add missing pieces, then report what was added.
5. If `installed`: read the active goal, bound todo, and latest chat log. Report the current state (goal summary, todo progress, pending tasks) and ask the user what they want to work on next. If `memorytree daemon status` shows the heartbeat is not registered, ask the user whether they want the recommended current-repository setup via `memorytree daemon quick-start --root <repo>` or only a machine-level scheduler restore via `memorytree daemon install --interval 5m --auto-push true`. Use `memorytree daemon register` only when they explicitly want custom branch, interval, report-port, or worktree settings. Use plain-text questions compatible with all AI assistants, not client-specific UI components.

Do not stop after detection to ask whether you should proceed. Act on the result immediately.

## Core Behavior

1. Detect the repo state before changing files. Use `references/project-detection.md`.
2. If MemoryTree is missing, initialize it with `memorytree init`. If the CLI is not available, create the files from `assets/templates/`.
3. If MemoryTree is partial, upgrade it with `memorytree upgrade` before manual maintenance.
4. If MemoryTree is already installed, maintain only the active goal, bound todo, and current chat log. Use `references/update-rules.md`.
5. Keep the installation compatible with the host repo's branch, PR, CI, and review rules. Use `references/git-policy.md`.
6. Prefer safe defaults: do not add reply suffix requirements unless the host repository already requires them, do not mix code-and-memory commits by default, and do not override branch policy. MemoryTree-only git automation is allowed only inside the isolated flow in `references/git-policy.md`.
7. When locale is not explicit, choose it from repo language first, then system language. Use `references/locale-selection.md`.
8. Keep reply language aligned with user language first, then repo locale. Use `references/response-language.md`.
9. For partial repos, use the non-destructive upgrade path before manual maintenance. Use `references/upgrade-path.md`.
10. When transcript archival is enabled, import transcripts with deterministic code, preserve raw transcripts as evidence in both the current repo mirror and the global archive, generate cleaned Markdown for indexing, keep cross-project backfills and ambiguous ownership cases in the global archive only, and ask once per repository whether raw transcript files may be committed or pushed. Use `references/transcript-archive.md`.
11. When CLI commands are needed, use `memorytree <subcommand>` (requires Node.js 鈮?20). If Node.js is not available, fall back to manual scaffolding from `assets/templates/`. See `references/execution-environment.md`.
12. Transcript discovery, import, cleaning, and push are handled by the background heartbeat process. The model only writes chat log summaries and updates goals and todos. See `references/heartbeat-scheduling.md`.
13. Global configuration is stored in `~/.memorytree/config.toml`. See `references/global-configuration.md`.
14. When the user asks to see their most recent conversation, trigger an on-demand transcript sync for the current project, locate the latest session across all three clients, and generate a continuation summary. See `references/transcript-archive.md` and `references/heartbeat-scheduling.md`.
15. All interactive prompts (heartbeat install, configuration, session continuity) must use plain-text questions compatible with every AI assistant that supports this skill. Do not rely on client-specific UI components. See `references/heartbeat-scheduling.md`.

## Read Order

1. Repo `AGENTS.md`, if present.
2. Latest file in `Memory/01_goals/`.
3. Latest todo bound to that goal in `Memory/02_todos/`.
4. `Memory/04_knowledge/` only when needed.
5. `Memory/06_transcripts/clean/`, transcript manifests, and repo-local raw transcript mirrors only when transcript history or cross-project memory search is relevant.
6. `Memory/03_chat_logs/` and `Memory/05_archive/` only when needed.

## Detect

1. Check whether `Memory/` exists and matches the layout in `references/memory-layout.md`.
2. Classify the repo as `not-installed`, `partial`, or `installed`.
3. If the repo already has stronger rules than the generated templates, preserve the repo rules and only add missing MemoryTree pieces.

## Upgrade

1. Use `memorytree upgrade` for repositories that already have `AGENTS.md`, custom policy files, or partial `Memory/` content.
2. Preserve existing repo policy files by default.
3. Create only the missing MemoryTree pieces.
4. Read the upgrade result and treat `agents_merge_required=true` as a manual review task, not an overwrite instruction.

## Initialize

1. Run `memorytree init --root <repo>` and pass `--project-name`, `--goal-summary`, and `--locale` when the user already provided them.
2. Use fresh init only when the repo does not already have `AGENTS.md` or another repo policy source such as a policy-bearing `CONTRIBUTING.md`, PR templates, `CODEOWNERS`, or commitlint config. If repo policy already exists, switch to `memorytree upgrade` instead of trying to skip `AGENTS.md`.
3. Review the generated `AGENTS.md` before keeping it. Merge it with the repo's existing policy if needed.
4. Keep the initial installation minimal: `Memory/01_goals`, `02_todos`, `03_chat_logs`, optional `04_knowledge`, `05_archive`, and `06_transcripts` only when transcript archival is enabled for the repo or needed for transcript import.
5. Use the locale-specific template files in `assets/templates/<locale>/` as the source of truth for first-run scaffolding.
6. Prefer `--locale auto` when the user did not request a language explicitly.
7. Use `memorytree locale` when you need a deterministic locale check without scaffolding files.
8. If Node.js is not available, create first-run files directly from `assets/templates/` instead of requiring a runtime installation.
9. If transcript archival is enabled for the repo, use `memorytree import --source <file>` for one explicit source file and `memorytree discover` when scanning local client stores. Matching transcripts must update both the repo mirror and the global archive, while unrelated projects, ambiguous ownership cases, or mismatched explicit sources are archived in the global archive only. Let the CLI generate cleaned transcripts deterministically without spending model tokens on the cleaning step.
10. Ask once whether raw transcript files may also be committed to the repository. Record the answer in `AGENTS.md`, keep the files in the repo either way, and exclude `raw` files from automatic staging until the user says yes.

## Maintain

1. Change the active goal only after explicit user confirmation of a scope or requirement change.
2. Update the active todo when progress changes, milestones move, or the next task becomes clearer.
3. Append chat logs only. Never rewrite or delete prior entries.
4. Keep active files small. Move stale context to archive or knowledge files instead of bloating the active goal or todo.
5. Treat product ideas, architecture decisions, and operating constraints as goal or knowledge content. Treat step-by-step execution state as todo content.
6. Treat cleaned transcript indexes as discovery aids, not as the final source of truth. When exact wording matters, confirm against the raw transcript archive.
7. Prefer deterministic CLI-based transcript cleaning over manual rewriting. Do not spend model tokens to restate or normalize transcript content when `memorytree import` can do it.
8. Reply in the user's language when clear; otherwise align with repo locale without rewriting existing files just to translate them.

## Git And Safety

1. Never assume MemoryTree can override the repo's branch model.
2. Default to isolated MemoryTree-only Git operations: stage only MemoryTree-owned files, use a MemoryTree-scoped commit title, push to a dedicated branch, and open a dedicated PR.
3. Enable auto-merge only for MemoryTree-only PRs, and only when the repository still enforces its required review and CI checks.
4. Keep repo-local raw transcript mirrors and the global transcript archive synchronized on every import. The global index must remain safe for concurrent multi-project updates.
5. Keep the repository mirror limited to transcripts that belong to the current repository. Unrelated or ambiguous transcripts belong in the global archive only.
6. Keep raw transcript files under `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` in the repo, but exclude them from automatic staging until the user explicitly approved raw transcript uploads for that repository.
7. If the diff mixes product code, shared policy files, cross-project transcript archives, or unclear ownership, stop and ask the user before committing or pushing.
8. If the repo has protected branches or PR-only rules, follow them even if older MemoryTree rules say otherwise.
9. When `auto_push` is enabled, the heartbeat process pushes automatically after committing. If no Git remote is configured, the push is skipped. If a push fails, the heartbeat retries once. In either case an alert is written to `~/.memorytree/alerts.json`. See `references/git-policy.md`.
10. During transcript cleaning, the heartbeat scans for sensitive information (API keys, passwords, tokens). Matches are logged as warnings only 鈥?no automatic deletion or redaction. See `references/heartbeat-scheduling.md`.

11. Do not modify the host repository's CI or E2E workflow definitions by default. If the user explicitly approves a MemoryTree-only optimization, prefer path-filtered or lightweight workflows for `Memory/**` and managed `AGENTS.md` PRs without weakening required branch protection.

## Resources

- `references/project-detection.md`: detect install state and choose init vs maintain.
- `references/memory-layout.md`: folder and file naming rules.
- `references/update-rules.md`: when to version goals, todos, and session logs.
- `references/git-policy.md`: safe Git defaults and policy merge guidance.
- `references/locale-selection.md`: locale choice rules and alias behavior.
- `references/response-language.md`: reply-language precedence and translation safety.
- `references/transcript-archive.md`: raw transcript archival, clean transcript indexing, per-client source rules, and repo upload confirmation rules.
- `references/upgrade-path.md`: safe adoption flow for partial repos.
- `references/execution-environment.md`: how to run MemoryTree CLI (requires Node.js 鈮?20).
- `references/heartbeat-scheduling.md`: background heartbeat architecture, daemon CLI, and execution flow.
- `references/global-configuration.md`: `~/.memorytree/` directory layout, `config.toml` schema, and `alerts.json` format.
- `assets/templates/en/` and `assets/templates/zh-cn/`: seed files for English and Simplified Chinese initialization.
- CLI commands: `memorytree init`, `memorytree upgrade`, `memorytree import`, `memorytree discover`, `memorytree locale`, `memorytree recall`, `memorytree daemon install|uninstall|run-once|watch|status|quick-start|register`.

        'sensitive_match',\r\n          `Sensitive pattern in transcript: ${basename(parsed.source_path)}`,\r\n        )\r\n        return\r\n      }\r\n    }\r\n  }\r\n}\r\n\r\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\r\n// Git operations\r\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\r\n\r\nexport function gitCommitAndPush(\r\n  config: Pick<Config, 'auto_push'>,\r\n  projectPath: string,\r\n  projectName: string,\r\n  importedCount: number,\r\n  rawUploadPermission: RawUploadPermission = 'not-set',\r\n): void {\r\n  const logger = getLogger()\r\n\r\n  const changedPaths = changedManagedPaths(projectPath)\r\n  if (changedPaths.length === 0) {\r\n    logger.info(`[${projectName}] No git changes in managed MemoryTree content.`)\r\n    return\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  const stageablePaths = changedPaths.filter(path => shouldStageManagedPath(path, rawUploadPermission))\r\n  if (stageablePaths.length === 0) {\r\n    logger.info(`[${projectName}] Only raw transcript mirror changes detected without approval; skipping commit.`)\r\n    return\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  const commitMessage = importedCount > 0\r\n    ? `memorytree(transcripts): import ${importedCount} transcript(s)`\r\n    : 'memorytree(snapshot): heartbeat sync'\r\n\r\n  git(projectPath, 'add', '-A', '-f', '--', ...stageablePaths)\r\n  git(projectPath, 'commit', '-m', commitMessage)\r\n  if (importedCount > 0) {\r\n    logger.info(`[${projectName}] Committed ${importedCount} transcript import(s).`)\r\n  } else {\r\n    logger.info(`[${projectName}] Committed heartbeat snapshot.`)\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  if (!config.auto_push) {\r\n    logger.info(`[${projectName}] auto_push disabled, skipping push.`)\r\n    return\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  const remotes = git(projectPath, 'remote')\r\n  if (!remotes.trim()) {\r\n    logger.warn(`[${projectName}] No git remote configured, skipping push.`)\r\n    writeAlert(toPosixPath(projectPath), 'no_remote', 'Push skipped: no Git remote configured.')\r\n    return\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  if (!tryPush(projectPath, projectName)) {\r\n    logger.warn(`[${projectName}] Push failed, retrying once...`)\r\n    if (!tryPush(projectPath, projectName)) {\r\n      logger.error(`[${projectName}] Push failed after retry.`)\r\n      writeAlertWithThreshold(toPosixPath(projectPath), 'push_failed', 'Push failed after retry.')\r\n      return\r\n    }\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  resetFailureCount(toPosixPath(projectPath), 'push_failed')\r\n}\r\n\r\nexport function tryPush(projectPath: string, projectName: string): boolean {\r\n  try {\r\n    const branch = currentBranch(projectPath)\r\n    if (hasTrackingUpstream(projectPath)) {\r\n      git(projectPath, 'push')\r\n    } else {\r\n      const upstream = ensureBranchUpstream(projectPath, branch)\r\n      if (upstream.remote === null) {\r\n        return false\r\n      }\r\n      getLogger().info(`[${projectName}] Configured upstream ${upstream.remote}/${branch}.`)\r\n    }\r\n    getLogger().info(`[${projectName}] Pushed successfully.`)\r\n    return true\r\n  } catch {\r\n    return false\r\n  }\r\n}\r\n\r\nexport function currentBranch(projectPath: string): string {\r\n  return git(projectPath, 'rev-parse', '--abbrev-ref', 'HEAD').trim()\r\n}\r\n\r\nexport function isDedicatedMemorytreeBranch(\r\n  branch: string,\r\n  project?: Pick<ProjectEntry, 'memory_branch'>,\r\n): boolean {\r\n  return isProjectMemoryBranch(branch, project)\r\n}\r\n\r\nexport function changedManagedPaths(projectPath: string): string[] {\r\n  const seen = new Set<string>()\r\n  const paths: string[] = []\r\n\r\n  for (const path of collectChangedManagedPaths(projectPath)) {\r\n    if (seen.has(path)) continue\r\n    seen.add(path)\r\n    paths.push(path)\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  return paths\r\n}\r\n\r\nexport function isRepoRawTranscriptPath(path: string): boolean {\r\n  return path.replace(/\\\\/g, '/').startsWith(RAW_TRANSCRIPT_PREFIX)\r\n}\r\n\r\nfunction shouldStageManagedPath(path: string, rawUploadPermission: RawUploadPermission): boolean {\r\n  if (!isRepoRawTranscriptPath(path)) {\r\n    return true\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  return rawUploadPermission === 'approved'\r\n}\r\n\r\nfunction unquotePath(path: string): string {\r\n  if (!(path.startsWith('\"') && path.endsWith('\"'))) return path\r\n\r\n  return path\r\n    .slice(1, -1)\r\n    .replace(/\\\\\"/g, '\"')\r\n    .replace(/\\\\\\\\/g, '\\\\')\r\n}\r\n\r\nfunction collectChangedManagedPaths(projectPath: string): string[] {\r\n  return [\r\n    ...gitPathLines(projectPath, 'diff', '--name-only', '--', ...MANAGED_REPO_PATHS),\r\n    ...gitPathLines(projectPath, 'diff', '--cached', '--name-only', '--', ...MANAGED_REPO_PATHS),\r\n    ...gitPathLines(projectPath, 'ls-files', '--others', '--exclude-standard', '--', ...MANAGED_REPO_PATHS),\r\n    ...gitPathLines(\r\n      projectPath,\r\n      'ls-files',\r\n      '--others',\r\n      '--ignored',\r\n      '--exclude-standard',\r\n      '--',\r\n      ...MANAGED_REPO_PATHS,\r\n    ),\r\n  ]\r\n}\r\n\r\nfunction gitPathLines(projectPath: string, ...args: string[]): string[] {\r\n  const output = git(projectPath, ...args)\r\n  const paths: string[] = []\r\n\r\n  for (const rawLine of output.split(/\\r?\\n/)) {\r\n    const path = unquotePath(rawLine.trim())\r\n    if (!path) continue\r\n    paths.push(path)\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  return paths\r\n}\r\n"],"mappings":";;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;AAKA,SAAS,YAAY,WAAW,cAAc,YAAY,qBAAqB;AAC/E,SAAS,eAAe;AACxB,SAAS,SAAS,eAAe;AAM1B,IAAM,aAAa;AASnB,IAAM,oBAAoB;AAmB1B,SAAS,aAAqB;AACnC,SAAO,QAAQ,QAAQ,GAAG,eAAe,aAAa;AACxD;AAEA,SAAS,mBAA2B;AAClC,SAAO,QAAQ,QAAQ,GAAG,eAAe,qBAAqB;AAChE;AAMA,SAAS,eAAuB;AAC9B,UAAO,oBAAI,KAAK,GAAE,YAAY,EAAE,QAAQ,aAAa,GAAG;AAC1D;AAMO,SAAS,aAA+B;AAC7C,QAAM,OAAO,WAAW;AACxB,MAAI,CAAC,WAAW,IAAI,GAAG;AACrB,WAAO,CAAC;AAAA,EACV;AACA,MAAI;AACF,UAAM,OAAO,aAAa,MAAM,OAAO;AACvC,UAAM,OAAgB,KAAK,MAAM,IAAI;AACrC,QAAI,CAAC,MAAM,QAAQ,IAAI,GAAG;AACxB,aAAO,CAAC;AAAA,IACV;AACA,WAAO;AAAA,EACT,QAAQ;AACN,WAAO,CAAC;AAAA,EACV;AACF;AAEO,SAAS,WAAW,SAAiB,WAAmB,SAAuB;AACpF,QAAM,SAAS,WAAW;AAC1B,QAAM,MAAM,aAAa;AAEzB,MAAI,QAAQ;AACZ,QAAM,UAAmB,CAAC;AAE1B,aAAW,SAAS,QAAQ;AAC1B,QAAI,MAAM,YAAY,WAAW,MAAM,SAAS,WAAW;AACzD,cAAQ,KAAK;AAAA,QACX,GAAG;AAAA,QACH,WAAW;AAAA,QACX;AAAA,QACA,QAAQ,MAAM,SAAS,KAAK;AAAA,MAC9B,CAAC;AACD,cAAQ;AAAA,IACV,OAAO;AACL,cAAQ,KAAK,EAAE,GAAG,MAAM,CAAC;AAAA,IAC3B;AAAA,EACF;AAEA,MAAI,CAAC,OAAO;AACV,YAAQ,KAAK,EAAE,WAAW,KAAK,SAAS,MAAM,WAAW,SAAS,OAAO,EAAE,CAAC;AAAA,EAC9E;AAEA,QAAM,UAAU,QAAQ,SAAS,aAC7B,QAAQ,MAAM,QAAQ,SAAS,UAAU,IACzC;AAEJ,aAAW,OAAO;AACpB;AAMO,SAAS,wBACd,SACA,WACA,SACM;AACN,QAAM,SAAS,kBAAkB;AACjC,QAAM,MAAM,GAAG,OAAO,KAAK,SAAS;AACpC,QAAM,WAAY,OAAO,GAAG,KAA4B,KAAK;AAC7D,QAAM,YAAoC,EAAE,GAAG,QAAQ,CAAC,GAAG,GAAG,QAAQ;AACtE,oBAAkB,SAAS;AAE3B,MAAI,WAAW,mBAAmB;AAChC,eAAW,SAAS,WAAW,OAAO;AAAA,EACxC;AACF;AAEO,SAAS,kBAAkB,SAAiB,WAAyB;AAC1E,QAAM,SAAS,kBAAkB;AACjC,QAAM,MAAM,GAAG,OAAO,KAAK,SAAS;AACpC,MAAI,OAAO,QAAQ;AACjB,UAAM,YAAoC,CAAC;AAC3C,eAAW,CAAC,GAAG,CAAC,KAAK,OAAO,QAAQ,MAAM,GAAG;AAC3C,UAAI,MAAM,KAAK;AACb,kBAAU,CAAC,IAAI;AAAA,MACjB;AAAA,IACF;AACA,sBAAkB,SAAS;AAAA,EAC7B;AACF;AAyCA,SAAS,WAAW,QAAgC;AAClD,QAAM,OAAO,WAAW;AACxB,YAAU,QAAQ,IAAI,GAAG,EAAE,WAAW,KAAK,CAAC;AAC5C,gBAAc,MAAM,KAAK,UAAU,QAAQ,MAAM,CAAC,IAAI,MAAM,OAAO;AACrE;AAMA,SAAS,oBAA4C;AACnD,QAAM,OAAO,iBAAiB;AAC9B,MAAI,CAAC,WAAW,IAAI,GAAG;AACrB,WAAO,CAAC;AAAA,EACV;AACA,MAAI;AACF,UA USER: "这几个文件是做什么的呢  必须放在根目录下吗"
ASSISTANT: "通俗讲，这 3 个文件都是“项目工具说明书”。\n\n不是业务功能代码，而是告诉测试工具、构建工具该怎么工作。\n\n**1. `vitest.config.ts`**\n这是“普通测试的说明书”。\n\n它告诉 Vitest：\n- 去哪里找测试\n- 哪些测试先别跑\n- 用什么全局设置\n\n你们现在这个文件的意思很简单：\n- 跑 `tests/**/*.test.ts`\n- 但排除 `tests/e2e/**`\n\n也就是：\n`npm test` 只跑普通单测和集成测，不跑 E2E。\n\n**2. `vitest.e2e.config.ts`**\n这是“E2E 测试的说明书”。\n\n它告诉 Vitest：\n- 只跑 `tests/e2e/**`\n- 不要并行跑\n- 超时时间给长一点\n\n因为 E2E 和普通单测不一样：\n- 更慢\n- 更依赖真实 CLI / 文件系统 / git / 端口\n- 并行容易互相打架\n\n所以它单独拆出来是合理的。\n\n**3. `tsup.config.ts`**\n这是“构建说明书”。\n\n它告诉 `tsup`：\n- 从哪个入口开始打包\n- 打包成什么格式\n- 目标 Node 版本是什么\n- 要不要清理旧产物\n- 要不要带 source map\n- CLI 文件开头要不要加 `#!/usr/bin/env node`\n\n你们现在的 `build` 命令其实就是靠它在工作。\n\n再回答你第二个问题：\n\n**必须放根目录吗？**\n`不是绝对必须，但默认最省事。`\n\n分开说：\n\n**`vitest.config.ts`**\n通常放根目录最自然，因为：\n- `vitest run` 默认就会在项目根找它\n- 团队和 CI 也最容易理解\n\n如果你非要挪位置，也可以，但通常要显式写：\n```bash\nvitest run --config path/to/xxx.ts\n```\n\n**`vitest.e2e.config.ts`**\n也不是必须在根目录。\n因为你们已经显式写了：\n```json\n\"test:e2e\": \"vitest run --config vitest.e2e.config.ts\"\n```\n所以理论上它可以挪到别的地方，只要脚本路径一起改。\n\n**`tsup.config.ts`**\n也不是硬性必须在根目录。\n但 `tsup` 默认就是优先在项目根找配置文件。\n如果挪走，就要改 `build` 脚本，比如指定配置路径。\n\n所以真实结论是：\n\n- `不是必须放根目录`\n- `但放根目录是 Node/TS 项目里最标准、最省心、最少出错的做法`\n\n你可以把它理解成：\n\n- 放根目录 =

147 ASSISTANT "可以，通俗讲就是 3 个层次。 **1. `transcript`** 就是“聊天记录采集和整理系统”。 它干的事是： - 去本机找 Claude Code、Codex、Gemini 的聊天记录 - 把原始记录保存起来 - 再清洗成适合人看的 Markdown - 建索引，方便以后搜索和回忆 你可以把它理解成： “把你和 AI 的对话，变成可沉淀、可检索的项目记忆原材料。” 对应你的理念，它解决的是： - 不丢聊天记录 - 不丢灵感 - 不同工具里的记录能归档到一起 - 当前项目的记录归当前项目，全局的记录归全局仓库 **2. `report`** 就是“把这些记忆做成一个可浏览的网站”。 它干的事是： - 把 `Memory/` 里的 goals、todos、knowledge、archive、transcripts - 生成一个静态 HTML 网站 - 你可以本地打开，也可以挂到 GitHub Pages 上 这个网站里现在已经有： - 首页 dashboard - transcript 列表 - 单条对话详情页 - goals / todos / knowledge / archive / projects 页面 - 搜索、标签、目录、面包屑、图谱、RSS 你可以把它理解成： “把原本散在文件夹里的记忆，变成一个能阅读、能查找、能分享的记忆门户。” **3. `heartbeat`** 就是“后台自动运行的整理器”。 它干的事是定时自动： - 扫描新聊天记录 - 导入 transcript - 清洗和归档 - 生成 report - 在合适的分支上提交 - 需要的话推送到远端 你可以把它理解成： “记忆系统的自动保洁员 / 自动归档员。” 没有它的话，你每次都得手工执行。 有了它，系统会自己持续整理。 **三者关系** 通俗一点： - `transcript` = 收集原材料 - `report` = 把原材料做成成品页面 - `heartbeat` = 自动持续生产 如果再贴近你想做的产品愿景： - `transcript` 负责“记住” - `report` 负责“看见” - `heartbeat` 负责“持续运转” 所以这三块合起来，实际上就是你说的那个“以 Git 仓库为底座的记忆系统”的核心骨架。 再用一句更白的话说： - 没有 `transcript`，你记不住 - 没有 `report`，你看不清 - 没有 `heartbeat`，你养不起 如果你愿意，我下一步可以继续很通俗地讲： “这 3 个东西在用户真实使用时，完整链路到底怎么跑一遍。”"

154 ASSISTANT "通俗讲，这 3 个文件都是“项目工具说明书”。 不是业务功能代码，而是告诉测试工具、构建工具该怎么工作。 **1. `vitest.config.ts`** 这是“普通测试的说明书”。 它告诉 Vitest： - 去哪里找测试 - 哪些测试先别跑 - 用什么全局设置 你们现在这个文件的意思很简单： - 跑 `tests/**/*.test.ts` - 但排除 `tests/e2e/**` 也就是： `npm test` 只跑普通单测和集成测，不跑 E2E。 **2. `vitest.e2e.config.ts`** 这是“E2E 测试的说明书”。 它告诉 Vitest： - 只跑 `tests/e2e/**` - 不要并行跑 - 超时时间给长一点 因为 E2E 和普通单测不一样： - 更慢 - 更依赖真实 CLI / 文件系统 / git / 端口 - 并行容易互相打架 所以它单独拆出来是合理的。 **3. `tsup.config.ts`** 这是“构建说明书”。 它告诉 `tsup`： - 从哪个入口开始打包 - 打包成什么格式 - 目标 Node 版本是什么 - 要不要清理旧产物 - 要不要带 source map - CLI 文件开头要不要加 `#!/usr/bin/env node` 你们现在的 `build` 命令其实就是靠它在工作。 再回答你第二个问题： **必须放根目录吗？** `不是绝对必须，但默认最省事。` 分开说： **`vitest.config.ts`** 通常放根目录最自然，因为： - `vitest run` 默认就会在项目根找它 - 团队和 CI 也最容易理解 如果你非要挪位置，也可以，但通常要显式写： ```bash vitest run --config path/to/xxx.ts ``` **`vitest.e2e.config.ts`** 也不是必须在根目录。 因为你们已经显式写了： ```json \"test:e2e\": \"vitest run --config vitest.e2e.config.ts\" ``` 所以理论上它可以挪到别的地方，只要脚本路径一起改。 **`tsup.config.ts`** 也不是硬性必须在根目录。 但 `tsup` 默认就是优先在项目根找配置文件。 如果挪走，就要改 `build` 脚本，比如指定配置路径。 所以真实结论是： - `不是必须放根目录` - `但放根目录是 Node/TS 项目里最标准、最省心、最少出错的做法` 你可以把它理解成： - 放根目录 = 工具一进门就能找到 - 挪别处 = 也行，但要专门告诉工具去哪找 如果你问我从工程管理角度怎么判断： - 小项目、单包仓库、一个 CLI：放根目录最好 - 多包 monorepo、配置特别多：才更有必要分目录整理 你们这个仓库目前更像前一种，所以放根目录是合理的，不丑，也不算乱。 一句话总结： - 这三个文件分别管“普通测试”“E2E 测试”“构建打包” - 它们不是必须在根目录 - 但对你们现在这个仓库来说，放根目录是最合适、最标准的方案 如果你愿意，我下一步可以继续只讨论： “将来如果项目变大，哪些配置文件值得挪，哪些最好永远留在根目录。”"

004 ASSISTANT "`#25` 做的功能，通俗讲就是： 本来你执行： - `memorytree init` - 或 `memorytree upgrade` 它只是在当前仓库里帮你建好 `Memory/`、`AGENTS.md` 这些文件。 `#25` 想再多做一步： 它会**顺手把这个仓库登记到你电脑的全局配置里**，也就是 `~/.memorytree/config.toml`。 这样一来，后台的 heartbeat 系统就会“知道有这个项目了”。 你可以把它理解成： - `init / upgrade`：先把房子装修好 - `register / quick-start`：再去物业登记，接入小区的自动服务 `#25` 的意思是：你装修房子的时候，我顺手帮你把物业登记也办了。 **那我们为什么说要重写，不建议原样合并？** 不是因为这个想法没用。 恰恰相反，这个功能方向是有价值的。 问题在于它现在的写法，有点“手伸太长了”。 **第一层意思** “用户只想 scaffold 仓库，不一定等于他想把这个仓库加入 heartbeat 管理。” 这句话的大白话就是： - 用户可能只是想先把项目目录搭起来 - 但他未必已经决定，要让这个项目进入后台自动管理 这里几个英文词我顺手翻一下： - `scaffold`：搭脚手架，意思就是“先把基础目录和文件创建出来” - `heartbeat`：这里不是医学上的心跳，是“后台定时运行的一套自动任务” - `register`：登记、注册 - `config`：配置文件 所以整句话翻成最通俗的中文就是： “有些人只是想先把项目框架建出来，不代表他已经同意让后台自动系统接管这个项目。” **为什么这会是个问题？** 因为 `#25` 把两件事混在一起了： 1. 建仓库里的文件 2. 改电脑上的全局配置 而且第二件事不是改当前仓库，是改你整台机器共用的配置。 这就有几个风险： - 用户没意识到这个命令会改全局设置 - 仓库初始化成功了，但全局配置写失败了，结果变成“半成功半失败” - 文档现在本来把这两步分开写，用户预期也是分开的 - 测试还没把这个新副作用覆盖好 **再用一个更生活化的比喻** 现在的 `#25` 有点像： “你来买一张地铁卡，我顺手帮你办了整个月票自动续费。” 有些人会觉得方便。 但也有人会说： “等等，我只是先办卡，还没决定要不要开自动续费啊。” 所以问题不是“自动续费没价值”，而是： “你不能默认我已经同意这一步。” **所以我们说的“重写”，不是把功能推翻** 而是说： “这个需求可以保留，但实现方式要更克制、更明确。” 比如更合理的改法可以是： - 方案 1：加一个明确开关 例如 `memorytree init --register-project` 这样用户自己选 - 方案 2：只在 `daemon quick-start` 里做注册 因为这个命令本来就是“接入后台自动化”的意思 - 方案 3：自动注册可以做，但失败时不要把整个 init/upgrade 搞成奇怪的半失败状态 最多提示用户：“仓库建好了，但全局注册没完成” **一句话总结** `#25` 的功能是： “让 `init/upgrade` 后，项目自动出现在全局配置里，省掉手动登记。” 我们想重写，不是因为它没用， 而是因为它现在把“建项目框架”和“接入后台自动管理”硬绑在一起了，这对用户来说有点太突然了。 如果你愿意，我下一步可以继续把： - `#25` 现在的写法 - 和“更合理的改法” 直接给你画成一个一看就懂的对比。"

93:     logger.warn(`No registered project matched: ${resolve(options.root)}`)
94:     return 1
95:   }
96: 
97:   const projects = targetProject ? [targetProject] : config.projects
98: 
99:   logger.info(`Heartbeat started. ${projects.length} project(s) selected.`)
100: 
101:   let nextConfig = config
102:   let configChanged = false
103:   const now = new Date()
104:   const runTimestamp = now.toISOString()
105: 
106:   for (const entry of projects) {
107:     const projectName = projectDisplayName(entry)
108:     const projectPath = resolve(projectExecutionPath(entry))
109:     const heartbeatDue = options.force === true || projectIsDue(entry, now)
110: 
111:     if (!heartbeatDue) {
112:       logger.debug(`[${projectName}] Not due yet, skipping.`)
113:       continue
114:     }
115: 
116:     try {
117:       const worktree = ensureProjectWorktree(entry)
118:       if (!existsSync(projectPath)) {
119:         logger.warn(`Project path does not exist, skipping: ${projectPath}`)
120:         continue
130:           `[${projectName}] Synced context to ${worktree.branch} ` +
131:           `(copied ${contextSync.copied}, deleted ${contextSync.deleted}).`,
132:         )
133:       }
134: 
135:       const extraManifestDirs = collectExtraManifestDirs(projectPath)
136:       await processProject(config, projectPath, projectName, entry, extraManifestDirs)
137:       nextConfig = noteProjectHeartbeatRun(nextConfig, entry.id, runTimestamp)
138:       configChanged = true
139: 
140:       const outputSync = syncProjectOutputsToDevelopment(entry)
141:       if (!outputSync.skipped) {
142:         logger.info(
143:           `[${projectName}] Synced outputs back to development directory ` +
144:           `(copied ${outputSync.copied}, deleted ${outputSync.deleted}).`,
145:         )
146:       }
147:     } catch (err: unknown) {
148:       logger.exception(`Error processing project: ${projectPath}`, err)
149:       writeAlertWithThreshold(
150:         toPosixPath(projectPath),
151:         'push_failed',
152:         `Heartbeat error for project: ${basename(projectPath)}`,
153:       )
154:     }
155:   }
156: 
157:   if (configChanged) {
158:     saveConfig(nextConfig)
159:   }
160: 
161:   logger.info('Heartbeat finished.')
162:   return 0
163: }
164: 
165: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
166: // Per-project processing
167: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
168: 
169: export async function processProject(
170:   config: Config,
171:   projectPath: string,
172:   projectName: string,
173:   project?: ProjectEntry,
174:   extraManifestDirs?: string[],
175: ): Promise<void> {
176:   const logger = getLogger()
177:   const repoSlug = slugify(projectName, 'project')
178:   const globalRoot = defaultGlobalTranscriptRoot()
179:   const branch = currentBranch(projectPath)
180:   const mirrorToRepo = isDedicatedMemorytreeBranch(branch, project)
181:   const autoPush = project?.auto_push ?? config.auto_push ?? true
182:   const generateReport = project?.generate_report ?? config.generate_report ?? false
183:   const aiSummaryModel = project?.ai_summary_model ?? config.ai_summary_model ?? 'claude-haiku-4-5-20251001'
184:   const locale = project?.locale ?? config.locale ?? 'en'
185:   const ghPagesBranch = project?.gh_pages_branch ?? config.gh_pages_branch ?? ''
186:   const cname = project?.cname ?? config.cname ?? ''
187:   const webhookUrl = project?.webhook_url ?? config.webhook_url ?? ''
188:   const reportBaseUrl = project?.report_base_url ?? config.report_base_url ?? ''
189:   const rawUploadPermission = project?.raw_upload_permission ?? 'not-set'
190: 
300:   const stageablePaths = changedPaths.filter(path => shouldStageManagedPath(path, rawUploadPermission))
301:   if (stageablePaths.length === 0) {
302:     logger.info(`[${projectName}] Only raw transcript mirror changes detected without approval; skipping commit.`)
303:     return
304:   }
305: 
306:   const commitMessage = importedCount > 0
307:     ? `memorytree(transcripts): import ${importedCount} transcript(s)`
308:     : 'memorytree(snapshot): heartbeat sync'
309: 
310:   git(projectPath, 'add', '-A', '-f', '--', ...stageablePaths)
311:   git(projectPath, 'commit', '-m', commitMessage)
312:   if (importedCount > 0) {
313:     logger.info(`[${projectName}] Committed ${importedCount} transcript import(s).`)
314:   } else {
315:     logger.info(`[${projectName}] Committed heartbeat snapshot.`)
316:   }
317: 
318:   if (!config.auto_push) {
319:     logger.info(`[${projectName}] auto_push disabled, skipping push.`)
320:     return
321:   }
322: 
323:   const remotes = git(projectPath, 'remote')
324:   if (!remotes.trim()) {
325:     logger.warn(`[${projectName}] No git remote configured, skipping push.`)
326:     writeAlert(toPosixPath(projectPath), 'no_remote', 'Push skipped: no Git remote configured.')
327:     return
328:   }
329: 
330:   if (!tryPush(projectPath, projectName)) {
331:     logger.warn(`[${projectName}] Push failed, retrying once...`)
332:     if (!tryPush(projectPath, projectName)) {
333:       logger.error(`[${projectName}] Push failed after retry.`)
334:       writeAlertWithThreshold(toPosixPath(projectPath), 'push_failed', 'Push failed after retry.')
335:       return
336:     }
337:   }
338: 
339:   resetFailureCount(toPosixPath(projectPath), 'push_failed')
340: }
341: 
342: export function tryPush(projectPath: string, projectName: string): boolean {
343:   try {
344:     const branch = currentBranch(projectPath)
345:     if (hasTrackingUpstream(projectPath)) {
346:       git(projectPath, 'push')
347:     } else {
348:       const upstream = ensureBranchUpstream(projectPath, branch)
349:       if (upstream.remote === null) {
350:         return false
351:       }
352:       getLogger().info(`[${projectName}] Configured upstream ${upstream.remote}/${branch}.`)
353:     }
354:     getLogger().info(`[${projectName}] Pushed successfully.`)
355:     return true
356:   } catch {
357:     return false
358:   }
359: }
360: 
361: export function currentBranch(projectPath: string): string {
362:   return git(projectPath, 'rev-parse', '--abbrev-ref', 'HEAD').trim()
363: }
364: 
365: export function isDedicatedMemorytreeBranch(
366:   branch: string,
367:   project?: Pick<ProjectEntry, 'memory_branch'>,
368: ): boolean {
369:   return isProjectMemoryBranch(branch, project)
370: }
371: 
372: export function changedManagedPaths(projectPath: string): string[] {
373:   const seen = new Set<string>()
374:   const paths: string[] = []
375: 
376:   for (const path of collectChangedManagedPaths(projectPath)) {
377:     if (seen.has(path)) continue
378:     seen.add(path)
379:     paths.push(path)
380:   }
381: 
382:   return paths
383: }
384: 
385: export function isRepoRawTranscriptPath(path: string): boolean {
386:   return path.replace(/\\/g, '/').startsWith(RAW_TRANSCRIPT_PREFIX)
387: }
388: 
389: function shouldStageManagedPath(path: string, rawUploadPermission: RawUploadPermission): boolean {
390:   if (!isRepoRawTranscriptPath(path)) {
391:     return true
392:   }
393: 
394:   return rawUploadPermission === 'approved'
395: }
396: 
397: function unquotePath(path: string): string {
398:   if (!(path.startsWith('"') && path.endsWith('"'))) return path
399: 
400:   return path
401:     .slice(1, -1)
402:     .replace(/\\"/g, '"')
403:     .replace(/\\\\/g, '\\')
404: }
405: 
406: function collectChangedManagedPaths(projectPath: string): string[] {
407:   return [
408:     ...gitPathLines(projectPath, 'diff', '--name-only', '--', ...MANAGED_REPO_PATHS),
409:     ...gitPathLines(projectPath, 'diff', '--cached', '--name-only', '--', ...MANAGED_REPO_PATHS),
410:     ...gitPathLines(projectPath, 'ls-files', '--others', '--exclude-standard', '--', ...MANAGED_REPO_PATHS),
411:     ...gitPathLines(
412:       projectPath,
413:       'ls-files',
414:       '--others',
415:       '--ignored',
416:       '--exclude-standard',
417:       '--',
418:       ...MANAGED_REPO_PATHS,
419:     ),
420:   ]
421: }
422: 
423: function gitPathLines(projectPath: string, ...args: string[]): string[] {
424:   const output = git(projectPath, ...args)
425:   const paths: string[] = []
426: 
427:   for (const rawLine of output.split(/\r?\n/)) {
428:     const path = unquotePath(rawLine.trim())
429:     if (!path) continue
430:     paths.push(path)

672: export function ensureGitignore(root: string, entry: string): void {
673:   const gitignorePath = join(root, '.gitignore')
674:   let existing = ''
675:   if (existsSync(gitignorePath)) {
676:     try {
677:       existing = readFileSync(gitignorePath, 'utf-8')
678:     } catch {
679:       return
680:     }
681:   }
682:   // Check if already present (normalize line endings)
683:   const lines = existing.replace(/\r\n/g, '\n').split('\n')
684:   if (lines.some(l => l.trim() === entry.trim())) return
685: 
686:   // Append with trailing newline
687:   const append = existing.endsWith('\n') ? entry + '\n' : '\n' + entry + '\n'
688:   try {
689:     appendFileSync(gitignorePath, append, 'utf-8')
690:   } catch {
691:     // Best-effort
692:   }
693: }

263:   const logger = getLogger()

+function stageManagedPaths(projectPath: string, stageablePaths: readonly string[]): void {
+  let batch: string[] = []
+  let batchChars = 0
+
+  for (const path of stageablePaths) {
+    const pathChars = path.length + 1
+    if (batch.length > 0 && batchChars + pathChars > MAX_GIT_ADD_PATH_CHARS) {
+      git(projectPath, 'add', '-A', '-f', '--', ...batch)
+      batch = []
+      batchChars = 0
+    }
+
+    batch.push(path)
+    batchChars += pathChars
+  }
+
+  if (batch.length > 0) {
+    git(projectPath, 'add', '-A', '-f', '--', ...batch)
+  }
+}

47:   /(?:sk-|pk_live_|sk_live_|ghp_|gho_|glpat-)\S{10,}/,
48:   /Bearer\s+\S{20,}/i,
49: ]

51: const RAW_TRANSCRIPT_PREFIX = 'Memory/06_transcripts/raw/'
52: const MAX_GIT_ADD_PATH_CHARS = 12_000
53: 
54: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
55: // Main entry point
56: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
57: 
58: export interface HeartbeatRunOptions {
59:   readonly force?: boolean
60:   readonly root?: string
300: 
301:   const stageablePaths = changedPaths.filter(path => shouldStageManagedPath(path, rawUploadPermission))
302:   if (stageablePaths.length === 0) {
303:     logger.info(`[${projectName}] Only raw transcript mirror changes detected without approval; skipping commit.`)
304:     return
305:   }
306: 
307:   const commitMessage = importedCount > 0
308:     ? `memorytree(transcripts): import ${importedCount} transcript(s)`
309:     : 'memorytree(snapshot): heartbeat sync'
310: 
311:   stageManagedPaths(projectPath, stageablePaths)
312:   git(projectPath, 'commit', '-m', commitMessage)
313:   if (importedCount > 0) {
314:     logger.info(`[${projectName}] Committed ${importedCount} transcript import(s).`)
315:   } else {
316:     logger.info(`[${projectName}] Committed heartbeat snapshot.`)
317:   }
318: 
319:   if (!config.auto_push) {
320:     logger.info(`[${projectName}] auto_push disabled, skipping push.`)
321:     return
322:   }
323: 
324:   const remotes = git(projectPath, 'remote')
325:   if (!remotes.trim()) {
326:     logger.warn(`[${projectName}] No git remote configured, skipping push.`)
327:     writeAlert(toPosixPath(projectPath), 'no_remote', 'Push skipped: no Git remote configured.')
328:     return
329:   }
330: 
331:   if (!tryPush(projectPath, projectName)) {
332:     logger.warn(`[${projectName}] Push failed, retrying once...`)
333:     if (!tryPush(projectPath, projectName)) {
334:       logger.error(`[${projectName}] Push failed after retry.`)
335:       writeAlertWithThreshold(toPosixPath(projectPath), 'push_failed', 'Push failed after retry.')
336:       return
337:     }
338:   }
339: 
340:   resetFailureCount(toPosixPath(projectPath), 'push_failed')
341: }
342: 
343: export function tryPush(projectPath: string, projectName: string): boolean {
344:   try {
345:     const branch = currentBranch(projectPath)
346:     if (hasTrackingUpstream(projectPath)) {
347:       git(projectPath, 'push')
348:     } else {
349:       const upstream = ensureBranchUpstream(projectPath, branch)
350:       if (upstream.remote === null) {
351:         return false
352:       }
353:       getLogger().info(`[${projectName}] Configured upstream ${upstream.remote}/${branch}.`)
354:     }
355:     getLogger().info(`[${projectName}] Pushed successfully.`)
356:     return true
357:   } catch {
358:     return false
359:   }
360: }
420:     ),
421:   ]
422: }
423: 
424: function stageManagedPaths(projectPath: string, stageablePaths: readonly string[]): void {
425:   let batch: string[] = []
426:   let batchChars = 0
427: 
428:   for (const path of stageablePaths) {
429:     const pathChars = path.length + 1
430:     if (batch.length > 0 && batchChars + pathChars > MAX_GIT_ADD_PATH_CHARS) {
431:       git(projectPath, 'add', '-A', '-f', '--', ...batch)
432:       batch = []
433:       batchChars = 0
434:     }
435: 
436:     batch.push(path)
437:     batchChars += pathChars
438:   }
439: 
440:   if (batch.length > 0) {
441:     git(projectPath, 'add', '-A', '-f', '--', ...batch)
442:   }
443: }
444: 
445: function gitPathLines(projectPath: string, ...args: string[]): string[] {
446:   const output = git(projectPath, ...args)
447:   const paths: string[] = []
448: 
449:   for (const rawLine of output.split(/\r?\n/)) {
450:     const path = unquotePath(rawLine.trim())
451:     if (!path) continue
452:     paths.push(path)
453:   }
454: 
455:   return paths
456: }

019d1ebe-f7c7-7b23-8b07-a53ec346f0b5__5e8efb22.jsonl
"你说得对，我刚才把 git 提交和历史会话混在一起了。现在按聊天记录来整理，不看提交历史。\n\n**历史会话里最值得保留的 10 个问题/修复点**\n1. 原始 JSONL 不能只“照抄成正文”，需要先结构化，再转成 Markdown/HTML，保证层级和可读性都在。\n2. `tool_result` / `function_call_output` 这类工具输出不能直接揉进 assistant 正文，否则 clean transcript 会被噪音污染。\n3. transcript 需要“证据化”保留，最好把可读内容和工具证据分层保存，而不是混成一段。\n4. `recall` 查询必须排除当前会话本身，必须依赖 activation time，不然会把这次对话也当成“最近一次”。\n5. `5m heartbeat` 和 `30m refresh` 的语义要分清楚，前者是常规同步节奏，后者不是另一套心跳，而是补充刷新语义。\n6. `init/upgrade` 后自动把项目写入全局配置，这个方向是对的，能减少用户手工配置成本。\n7. 本地 `memorytree` worktree / 分支要和主开发分离，避免 heartbeat 自动提交污染主分支工作区。\n8. GitHub Pages 可以自动发布报告，但 Pages 源的首次配置仍然有一次性手动步骤，不是完全零配置。\n9. `caddy status` 这类状态检查要正确带上允许的请求头，不然会出现“其实在跑，但状态误判 403”的假故障。\n10. 原始 transcript 的上传和提交要做权限控制，未批准时 `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` 只保留本地，不参与常规提交。\n\n**项目本质**\nMemoryTree Workflow 本质上是给 AI 编程仓库加一层“可持续记忆”：把对话、目标、待办、转录、报告和心跳同步串起来，让项目跨会话、跨客户端、跨机器都能延续上下文。README 里把它概括成“git-tracked project memory + transcript indexing + worktree-safe heartbeat + report publishing”，功能入口在 [README.md](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/README.md#L7) 和 [src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)。\n\n**功能核对**\n从 CLI 入口看，项目已经覆盖了 `init`、`upgrade`、`import`、`discover`、`locale`、`recall`、`report`、`caddy`、`daemon` 这些核心能力，分别对应工作区初始化、转录导入/发现、会话回溯、报告生成、Caddy 托管和 heartbeat 管理。[src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)  \n我也按功能跑了验证：`npm test` 通过了 710 个测试，`npm run typecheck` 通过了，`npm run test:e2e` 也通过了 24 个端到端测试，覆盖了 import/discover/recall/report serve/register/heartbeat/raw trans

"你说得对，我刚才把 git 提交和历史会话混在一起了。现在按聊天记录来整理，不看提交历史。\n\n**历史会话里最值得保留的 10 个问题/修复点**\n1. 原始 JSONL 不能只“照抄成正文”，需要先结构化，再转成 Markdown/HTML，保证层级和可读性都在。\n2. `tool_result` / `function_call_output` 这类工具输出不能直接揉进 assistant 正文，否则 clean transcript 会被噪音污染。\n3. transcript 需要“证据化”保留，最好把可读内容和工具证据分层保存，而不是混成一段。\n4. `recall` 查询必须排除当前会话本身，必须依赖 activation time，不然会把这次对话也当成“最近一次”。\n5. `5m heartbeat` 和 `30m refresh` 的语义要分清楚，前者是常规同步节奏，后者不是另一套心跳，而是补充刷新语义。\n6. `init/upgrade` 后自动把项目写入全局配置，这个方向是对的，能减少用户手工配置成本。\n7. 本地 `memorytree` worktree / 分支要和主开发分离，避免 heartbeat 自动提交污染主分支工作区。\n8. GitHub Pages 可以自动发布报告，但 Pages 源的首次配置仍然有一次性手动步骤，不是完全零配置。\n9. `caddy status` 这类状态检查要正确带上允许的请求头，不然会出现“其实在跑，但状态误判 403”的假故障。\n10. 原始 transcript 的上传和提交要做权限控制，未批准时 `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` 只保留本地，不参与常规提交。\n\n**项目本质**\nMemoryTree Workflow 本质上是给 AI 编程仓库加一层“可持续记忆”：把对话、目标、待办、转录、报告和心跳同步串起来，让项目跨会话、跨客户端、跨机器都能延续上下文。README 里把它概括成“git-tracked project memory + transcript indexing + worktree-safe heartbeat + report publishing”，功能入口在 [README.md](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/README.md#L7) 和 [src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)。\n\n**功能核对**\n从 CLI 入口看，项目已经覆盖了 `init`、`upgrade`、`import`、`discover`、`locale`、`recall`、`report`、`caddy`、`daemon` 这些核心能力，分别对应工作区初始化、转录导入/发现、会话回溯、报告生成、Caddy 托管和 heartbeat 管理。[src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)  \n我也按功能跑了验证：`npm test` 通过了 710 个测试，`npm run typecheck` 通过了，`npm run test:e2e` 也通过了 24 个端到端测试，覆盖了 import/discover/recall/report serve/register/heartbeat/raw trans

"你说得对，我刚才把 git 提交和历史会话混在一起了。现在按聊天记录来整理，不看提交历史。\n\n**历史会话里最值得保留的 10 个问题/修复点**\n1. 原始 JSONL 不能只“照抄成正文”，需要先结构化，再转成 Markdown/HTML，保证层级和可读性都在。\n2. `tool_result` / `function_call_output` 这类工具输出不能直接揉进 assistant 正文，否则 clean transcript 会被噪音污染。\n3. transcript 需要“证据化”保留，最好把可读内容和工具证据分层保存，而不是混成一段。\n4. `recall` 查询必须排除当前会话本身，必须依赖 activation time，不然会把这次对话也当成“最近一次”。\n5. `5m heartbeat` 和 `30m refresh` 的语义要分清楚，前者是常规同步节奏，后者不是另一套心跳，而是补充刷新语义。\n6. `init/upgrade` 后自动把项目写入全局配置，这个方向是对的，能减少用户手工配置成本。\n7. 本地 `memorytree` worktree / 分支要和主开发分离，避免 heartbeat 自动提交污染主分支工作区。\n8. GitHub Pages 可以自动发布报告，但 Pages 源的首次配置仍然有一次性手动步骤，不是完全零配置。\n9. `caddy status` 这类状态检查要正确带上允许的请求头，不然会出现“其实在跑，但状态误判 403”的假故障。\n10. 原始 transcript 的上传和提交要做权限控制，未批准时 `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` 只保留本地，不参与常规提交。\n\n**项目本质**\nMemoryTree Workflow 本质上是给 AI 编程仓库加一层“可持续记忆”：把对话、目标、待办、转录、报告和心跳同步串起来，让项目跨会话、跨客户端、跨机器都能延续上下文。README 里把它概括成“git-tracked project memory + transcript indexing + worktree-safe heartbeat + report publishing”，功能入口在 [README.md](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/README.md#L7) 和 [src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)。\n\n**功能核对**\n从 CLI 入口看，项目已经覆盖了 `init`、`upgrade`、`import`、`discover`、`locale`、`recall`、`report`、`caddy`、`daemon` 这些核心能力，分别对应工作区初始化、转录导入/发现、会话回溯、报告生成、Caddy 托管和 heartbeat 管理。[src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)  \n我也按功能跑了验证：`npm test` 通过了 710 个测试，`npm run typecheck` 通过了，`npm run test:e2e` 也通过了 24 个端到端测试，覆盖了 import/discover/recall/report serve/register/heartbeat/raw trans

"你说得对，我刚才把 git 提交和历史会话混在一起了。现在按聊天记录来整理，不看提交历史。\n\n**历史会话里最值得保留的 10 个问题/修复点**\n1. 原始 JSONL 不能只“照抄成正文”，需要先结构化，再转成 Markdown/HTML，保证层级和可读性都在。\n2. `tool_result` / `function_call_output` 这类工具输出不能直接揉进 assistant 正文，否则 clean transcript 会被噪音污染。\n3. transcript 需要“证据化”保留，最好把可读内容和工具证据分层保存，而不是混成一段。\n4. `recall` 查询必须排除当前会话本身，必须依赖 activation time，不然会把这次对话也当成“最近一次”。\n5. `5m heartbeat` 和 `30m refresh` 的语义要分清楚，前者是常规同步节奏，后者不是另一套心跳，而是补充刷新语义。\n6. `init/upgrade` 后自动把项目写入全局配置，这个方向是对的，能减少用户手工配置成本。\n7. 本地 `memorytree` worktree / 分支要和主开发分离，避免 heartbeat 自动提交污染主分支工作区。\n8. GitHub Pages 可以自动发布报告，但 Pages 源的首次配置仍然有一次性手动步骤，不是完全零配置。\n9. `caddy status` 这类状态检查要正确带上允许的请求头，不然会出现“其实在跑，但状态误判 403”的假故障。\n10. 原始 transcript 的上传和提交要做权限控制，未批准时 `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` 只保留本地，不参与常规提交。\n\n**项目本质**\nMemoryTree Workflow 本质上是给 AI 编程仓库加一层“可持续记忆”：把对话、目标、待办、转录、报告和心跳同步串起来，让项目跨会话、跨客户端、跨机器都能延续上下文。README 里把它概括成“git-tracked project memory + transcript indexing + worktree-safe heartbeat + report publishing”，功能入口在 [README.md](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/README.md#L7) 和 [src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)。\n\n**功能核对**\n从 CLI 入口看，项目已经覆盖了 `init`、`upgrade`、`import`、`discover`、`locale`、`recall`、`report`、`caddy`、`daemon` 这些核心能力，分别对应工作区初始化、转录导入/发现、会话回溯、报告生成、Caddy 托管和 heartbeat 管理。[src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)  \n我也按功能跑了验证：`npm test` 通过了 710 个测试，`npm run typecheck` 通过了，`npm run test:e2e` 也通过了 24 个端到端测试，覆盖了 import/discover/recall/report serve/register/heartbeat/raw trans

"你说得对，我刚才把 git 提交和历史会话混在一起了。现在按聊天记录来整理，不看提交历史。\n\n**历史会话里最值得保留的 10 个问题/修复点**\n1. 原始 JSONL 不能只“照抄成正文”，需要先结构化，再转成 Markdown/HTML，保证层级和可读性都在。\n2. `tool_result` / `function_call_output` 这类工具输出不能直接揉进 assistant 正文，否则 clean transcript 会被噪音污染。\n3. transcript 需要“证据化”保留，最好把可读内容和工具证据分层保存，而不是混成一段。\n4. `recall` 查询必须排除当前会话本身，必须依赖 activation time，不然会把这次对话也当成“最近一次”。\n5. `5m heartbeat` 和 `30m refresh` 的语义要分清楚，前者是常规同步节奏，后者不是另一套心跳，而是补充刷新语义。\n6. `init/upgrade` 后自动把项目写入全局配置，这个方向是对的，能减少用户手工配置成本。\n7. 本地 `memorytree` worktree / 分支要和主开发分离，避免 heartbeat 自动提交污染主分支工作区。\n8. GitHub Pages 可以自动发布报告，但 Pages 源的首次配置仍然有一次性手动步骤，不是完全零配置。\n9. `caddy status` 这类状态检查要正确带上允许的请求头，不然会出现“其实在跑，但状态误判 403”的假故障。\n10. 原始 transcript 的上传和提交要做权限控制，未批准时 `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` 只保留本地，不参与常规提交。\n\n**项目本质**\nMemoryTree Workflow 本质上是给 AI 编程仓库加一层“可持续记忆”：把对话、目标、待办、转录、报告和心跳同步串起来，让项目跨会话、跨客户端、跨机器都能延续上下文。README 里把它概括成“git-tracked project memory + transcript indexing + worktree-safe heartbeat + report publishing”，功能入口在 [README.md](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/README.md#L7) 和 [src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)。\n\n**功能核对**\n从 CLI 入口看，项目已经覆盖了 `init`、`upgrade`、`import`、`discover`、`locale`、`recall`、`report`、`caddy`、`daemon` 这些核心能力，分别对应工作区初始化、转录导入/发现、会话回溯、报告生成、Caddy 托管和 heartbeat 管理。[src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)  \n我也按功能跑了验证：`npm test` 通过了 710 个测试，`npm run typecheck` 通过了，`npm run test:e2e` 也通过了 24 个端到端测试，覆盖了 import/discover/recall/report serve/register/heartbeat/raw trans

"你说得对，我刚才把 git 提交和历史会话混在一起了。现在按聊天记录来整理，不看提交历史。\n\n**历史会话里最值得保留的 10 个问题/修复点**\n1. 原始 JSONL 不能只“照抄成正文”，需要先结构化，再转成 Markdown/HTML，保证层级和可读性都在。\n2. `tool_result` / `function_call_output` 这类工具输出不能直接揉进 assistant 正文，否则 clean transcript 会被噪音污染。\n3. transcript 需要“证据化”保留，最好把可读内容和工具证据分层保存，而不是混成一段。\n4. `recall` 查询必须排除当前会话本身，必须依赖 activation time，不然会把这次对话也当成“最近一次”。\n5. `5m heartbeat` 和 `30m refresh` 的语义要分清楚，前者是常规同步节奏，后者不是另一套心跳，而是补充刷新语义。\n6. `init/upgrade` 后自动把项目写入全局配置，这个方向是对的，能减少用户手工配置成本。\n7. 本地 `memorytree` worktree / 分支要和主开发分离，避免 heartbeat 自动提交污染主分支工作区。\n8. GitHub Pages 可以自动发布报告，但 Pages 源的首次配置仍然有一次性手动步骤，不是完全零配置。\n9. `caddy status` 这类状态检查要正确带上允许的请求头，不然会出现“其实在跑，但状态误判 403”的假故障。\n10. 原始 transcript 的上传和提交要做权限控制，未批准时 `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` 只保留本地，不参与常规提交。\n\n**项目本质**\nMemoryTree Workflow 本质上是给 AI 编程仓库加一层“可持续记忆”：把对话、目标、待办、转录、报告和心跳同步串起来，让项目跨会话、跨客户端、跨机器都能延续上下文。README 里把它概括成“git-tracked project memory + transcript indexing + worktree-safe heartbeat + report publishing”，功能入口在 [README.md](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/README.md#L7) 和 [src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)。\n\n**功能核对**\n从 CLI 入口看，项目已经覆盖了 `init`、`upgrade`、`import`、`discover`、`locale`、`recall`、`report`、`caddy`、`daemon` 这些核心能力，分别对应工作区初始化、转录导入/发现、会话回溯、报告生成、Caddy 托管和 heartbeat 管理。[src/cli/main.ts](D:/demo1/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/main.ts#L19)  \n我也按功能跑了验证：`npm test` 通过了 710 个测试，`npm run typecheck` 通过了，`npm run test:e2e` 也通过了 24 个端到端测试，覆盖了 import/discover/recall/report serve/register/heartbeat/raw trans
